Member of the Eighthto Tenth Lok Sabhas from1984 to 1996 and Twelfth Lok Sabha from1998 to1999 representing the Osmanabad Parliamentary Constituency of Maharashtra.Earlier, Shri Kamble was a Member of the Maharashtra LegislativeAssembly from1980 to 1984. During thisperiod, Shri Kamble served as aDeputy-Minister in the Government ofMaharashtra in the year 1982.Shri Kamble was a Member of theConsultative Committee of the Ministryof Oil and Natural Gas during the EighthLok Sabha. He was a Member of theConsultative Committee of the Ministryof Surface Transport and Committee onthe Welfare of Scheduled Castes andScheduled Tribes during the Ninth LokSabha. Shri Kamble was a Member ofthe Committee onEstimates; Committee onDefence; Committee on Absence of Members from the Sittingsof the House andthe Consultative Committee of the Ministry of Labour during the Twelfth LokSabha.", "22.02.201045An agriculturist by profession, ShriKamble fought for the rights of farmersand workedtirelessly inthe service of the people. Shri Kamble played asignificant role in developmental activitiesof his constituency.He served astheChairman of the Leather Industries Development Corporation, Maharashtra duringthe year 1982.Shri Arvind TulsiramKamble passed away on 28thDecember, 2009 at Pune,Maharashtra at the age of 58.Shri Nageshwar Dwivedi was a Member of the Fourth and Fifth LokSabhas from1967 to 1977 representing the Machhlishahr ParliamentaryConstituency of Uttar Pradesh.Earlier, Shri Dwivedi was a Member of the Uttar Pradesh LegislativeAssembly from 1952 to1962 for two terms.An agriculturist by profession, ShriDwivedi took active part in the freedommovement. He participated in the Salt Satyagraha Movement and was imprisonedon a number of occasions.A well-known social and political worker, Shri Dwivedi was a Member ofDistrict Board, Jaunpur, from1948 to 1952. He was also a Member of UttarPradesh Khadi and GramodyogBoard from1963 to 1966 and Gramodyog Samitifrom1967 to1970.A Gandhian to the core, Shri Dwivediworked for the propagation of Khadiand Village Industries in rural areas through the Samagra Gram Seva Sangh; hefounded Shri Keshav Library in 1937 and served as its Manager from 1937 to1952. He was instrumental inthe establishment of theRashtriya Inter College atSujanganj. He also founded a Junior High School, a High School and an InterCollege in Belwar, Jaunpur.Shri Nageshwar Dwivedi passed away on 1stJanuary, 2010, atMachhlishahr, Uttar Pradesh at the age of 93.", "22.02.201046Shri JagpalSingh wasa Member ofthe Seventh Lok Sabha from1980 to1984 and Ninth Lok Sabhafrom1989 to1991, representing HardwarParliamentary Constituency of Uttar Pradesh, now in Uttarakhand.Shri Singh was a Member of the Committee of Privileges and the AdvisoryCommittee of the Ministry of Home Affairs during the Seventh Lok Sabha. Hewas a Member of the Consultative Committee of the Ministryof Information andBroadcasting during the Ninth Lok Sabha.An agriculturist by profession, Shri Singh worked for theuplift of poor andmarginalized sections of the society.He was associated with the Labour andIndianTrade Union movement. Shri JagpalSingh strove for rights of the studentsand courted arrest on numerousoccasions for their cause.Shri JagpalSingh passed away on 13thJanuary, 2010, at New Delhi at theage of 62.Shri Virdhi Chander Jain was a Member ofthe Seventh and Eighth LokSabhas from 1980 to 1989 representing the Barmer Parliamentary Constituency ofRajasthan.Earlier, Shri Jain was a Member ofthe Rajasthan Legislative Assemblyfrom1967 to1980.Shri Jainwas Memberof the Committee on Absence of Members from theSittings of the House; Joint Committeeon Offices of Profit and Joint Committeeon Salaries and Allowancesof Members of Parliament during the Seventh LokSabha. He was a Member of the Committee on Government Assurances during theEighth Lok Sabha.An advocate by profession, Shri Jainfought for the cause of the oppressedand the downtrodden.He struggled valiantlyfor the eradication of dacoit menacein his constituency. He worked untiringly for the cause of agriculturists. Shri Jainwas instrumental in eradicating social evils like \342\200\234Begar\342\200\235 and in the introduction of\342\200\234Baghori\342\200\235 (cash rent) in BarmerDistrict of Rajasthan.", "22.02.201047An active social and political worker,Shri Jain served as Member, BarmerNagarpalika, from 1950 to 1953; Pramukh,Barmer Zila Parishad for two termsfrom 1959 to 1964. Healso served as the President of the Bharat Sewak Samaj,Barmer District for over two decades.Shri VirdhiChander Jain passed away on 13thJanuary,2010, at Barmer atthe age of 89.Shri Ram Niwas Mirdha was a Memberofthe EighthLok Sabha from 1984to 1989 and Tenth Lok Sabha from1991to 1996 representing the Nagaur andBarmer Parliamentary Constituencies of Rajasthan respectively.He was also a Member of the Rajya Sabha from 1967 to 1984 for fourterms representing the State of Rajasthan.During his long and illustrious politicalcareer of almost three decades anda half, Shri Mirdha ably served asa Member of various Parliamentary Committees.He was the Chairman of the Joint Committee to Enquire into Irregularities inSecurities and Banking Transactionsduring the Tenth Lok Sabha.Earlier, Shri Mirdha was a member ofthe Rajasthan Legislative Assemblyfrom1953 to 1967. During this period, heserved as the Minister for Agriculture,Irrigation and Transport inthe Government of Rajasthan from 1954 to 1957.Thereafter, Shri Mirdha rose to assume the august Office of the Speaker of theRajasthan Legislative Assembly which office he ably servedfrom 1957to 1967.An astute administrator, Shri Mirdhaheld several important portfolios inthe Union Cabinet. Heservedas the Union Minister of State in the Ministry ofHome Affairs from June 1970 to March 1971 and thenagain fromMarch to June1986; Minister of State in the Department of Personnel and AdministrativeReforms from August 1970 to October 1974; Minister of State, DefenceProduction in the Ministry ofDefencefrom October, 1974 to December 1975;Minister of State in the Ministry ofSupply and Rehabilitation from December1975 to March 1977;Minister of State(Independent Charge) in the Ministry ofIrrigation from January 1983 to August 1984;Minister of State in the Ministry of", "22.02.201048External Affairs from August to December 1984; Minister of State (IndependentCharge) in the Ministry of Communicationsfrom December 1984to October 1986;Minister of State (Independent Charge) inthe Ministry of Textiles from October1986 to February1988; Minister of State (Independent Charge) in the Ministry ofWater Resources from November 1987 toFebruary 1988; Minister of Textilesfrom February 1988 to December 1989 and Minister of Health and FamilyWelfare from January to December 1989.Shri Mirdha adorned the Office ofthe Deputy Chairman, Rajya Sabha fromMarch 1977 to April 1980.A patron of arts and a sports enthusiast, Shri Mirdha was closely associatedwith various cultural and sportsbodiesand institutions in the country. He wasChairman, Lalit Kala Akademi; Honorary President, World Federation of UnitedNations Association and President, Youth Hostels Association of India, IndianHeritage Society and Rajasthan SansthanSangh. He alsoserved as the Chairman,National Institute of Sports and theDelhi Urban ArtsCommission; DeputyChairman, Special Organizing Committee for Ninth Asian Games and thePresident, Maharaja Surajmal Educational Society.A widelytravelled person, Shri Mirdha was a Member of the IndianParliamentary delegation tothe Commonwealth Parliamentary Conference held inOttawa, Canada in September 1977 and inWellington, New Zealand in November1979. He was also a member of the IndianParliamentary delegation tothe Inter-Parliamentary Union Conferenceheld inCaracas, Venezuela in September 1979.He was also the Leader oftheIndianDelegation toUnited Nations GeneralAssembly in September 1984.", "22.02.201049Shri RamNiwas Mirdha passed away on 29thJanuary, 2010at NewDelhiat the age of 85 after a brief illness.Hon. Members, you are all aware of thesad demise of Shri Jyoti Basu,former Chief Minister of West Bengal.An astute administrator, Shri Basuhas the unique distinction of being thelongest serving Chief Minister in the country. He was the Chief Minister of WestBengal for more than 23 years, that is from June, 1977to November, 2000.  AstheChief Minister of West Bengal, heworked steadfastlyfor the all-rounddevelopment of the State and introduced land reforms. A strong votary ofdecentralisation of power, hestrengthened the Panchayati Raj system in the State.He rendered a yeoman service for the welfare and uplift of the weak and thedowntrodden sections of the society.In his long and distinguished politicalcareer, ShriJyoti Basu\342\200\231s stint as alegislator began whenhe was elected to the Bengal Legislative Assembly in 1946,and he continued to be its membertill 2001 except for a short period from 1972 to1977. He made his mark as the Leaderof the Opposition in the West BengalLegislative Assembly between 1957 and 1967. He was twice the Deputy ChiefMinister of West Bengal between 1967 and 1970.Shri Basu, one of the pioneers of the Communist movement in India, was aleading figure in the Indiantradeunionmovement. He was the Vice-President ofthe CITU since its inception in 1970.A multifaceted personality, Shri Basu was also an accomplished author. Hepenned a large numberof essays in Bengali language which have been compiledand published in five volumes.Even after demitting the office of the Chief Minister owing to his frailhealth, ShriBasu continuedto remain actively associatedwith several projects forthe welfare of people.", "22.02.201050In his demise the country has losta worthy son and a committed votary ofthe humanitarian values and a legislatorpar excellence. His administrative acumenand political sagacityhave left an indelible imprint upon the political canvas ofthis country. His absence will always be felt in many walks of life.Shri Jyoti Basu passed away on 17thJanuary, 2010 at Kolkata at the age of95 after a brief illness.We deeplymourn the loss of these friends and I amsure the House wouldjoin me in conveyingour condolences to the bereaved families.Hon. Members, on 13thFebruary, 2010, in a cowardly terrorist attack, 15people including foreigners were killedand 60 others injured when a bombexploded at a popular bakery in the city ofPune. In a brutal naxal attack at theSilda camp of Eastern Frontier Riflesin West Midnapore, West Bengal on 15thFebruary, 2010, twenty paramilitary personnel were killed. Inyet another mindlessattack on 18thFebruary, 2010, naxalites struck Phulwari village in Bihar\342\200\231s JamuiDistrict killing around 11 villagers.The Housestrongly condemns these dastardly attackswhich are aimed atdisturbing the peace and creating chaos in the country. I am sure the House wouldjoin me in empathising inthis hour of griefwith the members of the families whobecame victims of these attacks.The House may now stand insilence for a short while as a mark of respectto the memory ofthe departed.12.43 hrs.The Members then stood insilence for a short while", "22.02.20105112.44 hrsPAPERS LAID ON THE TABLEMADAM SPEAKER:Now Papersto belaid.
